<span id="freeTextContainer8367804838412805008">These books would be so much better if the author just told the story and stopped trying to force feed beliefs down your throat. <br/><br/>For example, in this delightful romp, Richard met a sole man from a far off land who Richard gave many a lecture to about the value of life. <br/><br/>Then Richard met some of this man's village mates and had a chapter + giving the same lectures to all of them about the value of life. <br/><br/>THEN he met some of the wise men of the man's people and told the same lectures again!!!<br/><br/>Plus th</span>
  <span id="freeText8367804838412805008" style="display:none">These books would be so much better if the author just told the story and stopped trying to force feed beliefs down your throat. <br /><br />For example, in this delightful romp, Richard met a sole man from a far off land who Richard gave many a lecture to about the value of life. <br /><br />Then Richard met some of this man's village mates and had a chapter + giving the same lectures to all of them about the value of life. <br /><br />THEN he met some of the wise men of the man's people and told the same lectures again!!!<br /><br />Plus there were refresher lectures in-between and after all these main lectures. I can only assume that Terry Goodkind thinks his audience is excessively stupid (and given his interviews I think that is it).<br /><br />For those of you who are curious I will summarize the lectures in three brief points:<br /><br />- if you value your life you will be willing to fight for it.<br />- not making a choice or choosing not to fight is actually helping the enemy<br />- there's no compromise with people who rape, torture, and/or murder<br /><br />Also it should be noted that for this book and all others, one should remember that Richard is always the most right and it is always his way or the highway. But honestly if it gets him to shut up then I definitely support agreeing with whatever the hell he says. <br /><br />Aside from all the lectures the story was fairly enjoyable. Plus Goodkind has toned down the excessive rape and violence towards women and descriptions of how traumatized they are to the occasional one liners.</span>

<div id="review_1137312219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1137312219" />
    <a title="Lindsey Roberts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36974730-lindsey-roberts"><img alt="Lindsey Roberts" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1137312219?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey Roberts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey Roberts" href="/user/show/36974730-lindsey-roberts">Lindsey Roberts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1137312219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15324281754635116564">Naked Empire is the next in the Sword of Truth series by Terry Goodkind. I feel like I am running out of ways to praise this series. I can’t remember if there has ever been one where I have been so impatient for the next book every single time I have finished one and am just grateful that I have joined the library here so I can have access to them.<br/><br/>Naked Empire sees Richard and Kahlan journeying further into the Old World, not through a matter of choice but through one of necessity. Not only is R</span>
  <span id="freeText15324281754635116564" style="display:none">Naked Empire is the next in the Sword of Truth series by Terry Goodkind. I feel like I am running out of ways to praise this series. I can’t remember if there has ever been one where I have been so impatient for the next book every single time I have finished one and am just grateful that I have joined the library here so I can have access to them.<br /><br />Naked Empire sees Richard and Kahlan journeying further into the Old World, not through a matter of choice but through one of necessity. Not only is Richard’s gift slowly beginning to get the better of him, but more people have come to the realisation that he alone can be the ones to free them – and go about securing his help in all the wrong ways. I wasn’t sure on the last book because of the way it spent so little time with the main characters. However, it did mean that when reading this one, I felt like I knew the character of Jensen well rather than trying to adapt to her. Considering her role in the story, it was nice to not feel like her character was being forced upon us.<br /><br />What makes this book pick up again compared to the last was the way that it went back to the same format of the previous books. We follow the main characters for a while, but then get to see what is happening with the others as well. The chapters flick between the different parts of the world in order to explain what is going on there and it makes you engaged and gripped in the story throughout the entire book. If things are going well for one set of people, then something would be going wrong with the others.<br /><br />I can’t remember the last time a book put a smile on my face the way this one did. Just as you think everything is over and they have lost, Goodkind has one final twist that introduces elements that you think were long forgotten. His construction of his world is seamless – events that haven’t been mentioned for several books suddenly reappear – and not in a way that makes you think you’ve missed something. It’s like you too are greeting old friends and their arrival put a smile on my face that I couldn’t quite explain.<br /><br /><br />The last book made me doubtful as to whether the series was looking its grip slightly. But I have to admit, this one put me firmly back in my fan spot, wanting the next and cursing the fact that I have to wait until I can get hold of it. What else would make me forget to write my essay for a night other than Goodkind’s masterpiece? A truly engaging tale of magic and adventure, of love and sacrifice. Another truly amazing read and I can’t wait to get into the next one and see what whirlwind of adventure we will be spun on next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15324281754635116564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2840215683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2840215683" />
    <a title="Scott Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4606766-scott-johnson"><img alt="Scott Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291859320p2/4606766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2840215683?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Johnson" href="/user/show/4606766-scott-johnson">Scott Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4606766-scott-johnson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4606766-scott-johnson?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2840215683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12273667899770068370">Where to begin with this garbage fire....<br/><br/>I'm using a list because, similar to Goodkind, I can't come up with anything coherent to string everything together in a satisfying way.<br/><br/>1) There is less rape than usual. The bar is set so low now. There's not any explicit rape, this time, if I recall correctly, just lots of references to the Order systematically raping this new group of "pristinely ungifted" to breed more of them. "Just" that kind of horribleness.<br/><br/>2) Pacifists. While reading this, and know</span>
  <span id="freeText12273667899770068370" style="display:none">Where to begin with this garbage fire....<br /><br />I'm using a list because, similar to Goodkind, I can't come up with anything coherent to string everything together in a satisfying way.<br /><br />1) There is less rape than usual. The bar is set so low now. There's not any explicit rape, this time, if I recall correctly, just lots of references to the Order systematically raping this new group of "pristinely ungifted" to breed more of them. "Just" that kind of horribleness.<br /><br />2) Pacifists. While reading this, and knowing nothing about this series beyond what I've talked about in previous reviews, I knew this was Goodkind's first post-9/11 book. Sure enough, Pillars of Creation was published November 2001, but that means it was actually written pre-9/11, since he didn't write that thing in 2 months. There is such an obvious tone shift that my first thought was to check the publication dates.<br /><br />Once again, the political screed becomes unbearably blunt. Over and over and over and over we have Richard blathering on about how, basically, anyone who is a victim has only themselves to blame because their ideology is weak and they should just stand up for themselves and kill people.<br /><br />There is no gray area here, if you are a pacifist who does not want to perpetuate the cycle of violence, you are just as bad as the people violently raping everyone. He is enraged by people telling them stories about attempting to appease invaders to try to avoid their entire village being slaughtered, WHICH MAKES PERFECT SENSE IF THEY HAVE NEVER HAD TO FIGHT A DAY IN THEIR LIVES.<br /><br />I repeat "over" so many times because literally every time this comes up it results in rehashing almost word for word the same points, and Richard says them the same 2 or 3 different ways in the same paragraphs of dialogue, in case you're too stupid to get the message the first time.<br /><br />This segues nicely into....<br /><br />3) Richard isn't even a Mary Sue anymore, let alone a real character. He is just a megaphone for Goodkind to shout through. Everything Richard does has overtones of judging those around him and finding their ideologies and actions wanting. Actually, that's not even correct, because there is nothing those overtones would go over, it is the entirety of his character at this point.<br /><br />He just walks into a new region of this land (again), judges their culture as weak and unworthy, and in five minutes shows everyone how all you had to do was sharpen some sticks and you can free yourselves from the invading empire that conquered you.<br /><br />The entire driving force behind this "plot", the poison given to Richard, turns out to be completely pointless, because 5 minutes before he dies from it he can suddenly just blurt out instructions for unskilled followers to create a complex antidote. He drinks it and is better within 2 sentences, and the entire book's ticking clock is disarmed with the cliched 1 second remaining WITH NO ACTUAL EFFORT OR ANY SKILL THAT WAS EARNED OR ACQUIRED.<br /><br />I can't stress how lazy that is enough. This super effective and dangerous poison A) Does not hinder Richard in any way, its effects are only superficial and only relevant when they're being described as happening; and B) is resolved in 2 pages in the last 2% of the book by our "hero" getting another fucking deus ex machina where his gift just spontaneously "guided him" to the right ingredients.<br /><br />And that's on top of 7 books of establishing this "balance" that must be achieved with his powers, in the weird form of not eating meat to compensate for murdering people. Suddenly, there is an epiphany that he has been laboring under this false assumption and THAT is causing the problems with his gift......because he is infallible and his killing has always been justified, and he was wrong for believing he needed to atone for it!<br /><br />4) We've finally come right out and said it: Nothing Richard does is ever wrong. He is always justified in killing to achieve his goals and his reward is all the beef jerky he can eat.<br /><br />Not only is this just casually negated to serve the plot now, but it also goes against everything a character should be. He's supposed to be flawed, not infallible. He should feel conflicted as a hero forced to resort to violence, not be a justifiably righteous executioner.<br /><br />5) The writing has gotten, if possible, even worse. <br /><br />EDIT: I almost forgot NICHOLAS THE SLIDE. Doesn't that name just chill you to the deepest darkest corners of your soul? Also, this fucker was built up as invincible and world-ending....and nothing happened.<br /><br />This first quote is from earlier in the book, and is just the most ridiculous description I've ever seen after a line of dialogue...<br /><br /><blockquote>"I think he's waking," a man said in a subservient voice.</blockquote><br /><br />A subserviant voice :|<br /><br />Here's a sentence that almost made me throw my Kindle across the room....<br /><br /><blockquote>He reasoned that it was probably the result of whatever vile substance it was they had soaked the rag in to cause him to pass out when held over his face.</blockquote><br /><br />No shit. I just love how he can't say, "Must have been that shit on the rag," he has to remind you that there was a rag soaked in a substance that was held over his face and caused him to pass out, in case you forgot what happened a page ago.<br /><br />I highlighted two sentences later on in the book, around where Zedd sets off the "sunset spell" that....accomplishes nothing and is entirely meaningless except as an artificial suspense device. This is undermined, by the way, by them just walking out of the tent, saying where they're all going, and then just....leaving. There is no dramatic escape, they state their plan and then, indeed, carry it out with zero complications.<br /><br />Anyway, the quotes....<br /><br /><blockquote>She gave him a brief, brave smile.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>Zedd looked over his shoulder. Adie wore a beautiful, tearful smile. He couldn't remember the last time he had seen her smile.</blockquote><br /><br />Let me help you, Zedd: IT WAS TWO FUCKING PAGES AGO.<br /><br />Here's a revelation about Richard's gift:<br /><br /><blockquote>"I guess so. It does that -- it works sometimes to warn me."</blockquote><br /><br />When convenient to the plot, Richard now has Spidey-Sense built into his gift. Other times, like the 14,000 times he's been captured, it doesn't work.<br /><br /><br />Just....fuck this guy and fuck this book. Even ignoring the hateful political ideology evident throughout, again we have a book where nothing happens until about 80% through. The bulk of this book is nothing but constructing elaborate straw men to knock down in the last 20%. What little plot you can distill out of the "action" here is mostly irrelevant and nothing is accomplished....<br /><br />We start the book with the Wizard's Keep and surrounding city held by our heroes' faction....and it ends that way.<br /><br />We start the book with this hidden empire of "pristinely ungifted" independent and not affecting anything else in the world.....and it ends that way.<br /><br />None of our main characters' status changes other than an irrelevant change in geographic location (because, AGAIN, characters traverse this entire continent in mere pages). None of our characters risk anything other than a superficial threat to their health/safety, and none of them lose or gain anything (except for Richard who can now eat meat!).<br /><br />NOTHING. HAPPENS. The larger plot does not advance, characters do not grow or change their circumstances.<br /><br />This is nothing but a Very Special Episode (TM) about the dangers of pacifism.<br /><br />Jesus fucking christ why did I pick this series up again, this might actually be worse than Twilight at this point.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12273667899770068370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1224279164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10675131421036118044">Only gave this one three stars, mostly because of how many pages there were devoted to Richard explaining over and over why the Bandakar way of thinking was erroneous and the Bandakar arguing with him on why it was not before suddenly, almost simplistically deciding to agree with him.<br/><br/>I have to say I was also a teensy bit let down that the solution to Richard's magic out of balance problem was simply a matter of believing in himself, in being the Seeker, and in fighting against Jagang and the Imp</span>
  <span id="freeText10675131421036118044" style="display:none">Only gave this one three stars, mostly because of how many pages there were devoted to Richard explaining over and over why the Bandakar way of thinking was erroneous and the Bandakar arguing with him on why it was not before suddenly, almost simplistically deciding to agree with him.<br /><br />I have to say I was also a teensy bit let down that the solution to Richard's magic out of balance problem was simply a matter of believing in himself, in being the Seeker, and in fighting against Jagang and the Imperial Order. The whole he can eat meat thing... well, let's just say his suddenly being okay with it seemed odd given that he gave up eating meat and even cheese because these foods began tasting odd to him. They no longer tasted good and he had trouble stomaching them. This was not a conscious choice on his part and it was only later he learned about the whole balance in all things deal. Quickly being able to stomach the smell and taste because he's accepted that killing is necessary doesn't really fit with how he first came to stop eating these particular foods. *shrug*<br /><br />At least I understand now why Betty the goat was a part of the story for as long as she's been. I know Jennson was bonded with Betty and a connection to her mother but when time is of an essence and dangers abound on the journey, having a goat tagging along didn't seem the best of choices. Now that I know she served as an important aspect of the plot, I better understand. Of course, if Betty were mine and like family, I'd have been covorting hither and yon with her as well rather than leaving her behind when I didn't know anyone or trust many and would have no idea if I'd be able to return for her. <br /><br />It does seem as though Drefan and the fact that he did have some sort of healing skill that seems tied to at least a low level of magic has been forgotten. Not enough emphasis was made that some offspring might have the spark but only a very low level of it and therefore not considered gifted. That two half-brothers were both homocidal maniacs with mother issues also was never addressed though perhaps will be in a later book. The father was a killer with a desire to be all powerful and we know two of his sons were similar in outlook. Does this speak to a disorder that can be passed along but isn't necessarily passed to all children, such as a tendency for schizophrenia is in some families? Might be interesting to know. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10675131421036118044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2702416353" />
    <a title="Daniel Beckwith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19969642-daniel-beckwith"><img alt="Daniel Beckwith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484681663p2/19969642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2702416353?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Beckwith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Beckwith" href="/user/show/19969642-daniel-beckwith">Daniel Beckwith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2702416353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17813434824401797681">OK there were two big problems with this book.<br/><br/>first off YOUR FUCKING WITH THE LORE OF THE SWORD!!! WTF! If Richard doesn't beleive in the sword than he can;t kill with it... theres no BS about the anger going away and he being able to just use it like a normal ass sword. if he doesn't beleive in it, he can't hit anything with it.<br/>come on now.. i don't mind terry changing up shit like that for the point of the story, but you better god damn acknowledge that theres something funky going on with the</span>
  <span id="freeText17813434824401797681" style="display:none">OK there were two big problems with this book.<br /><br />first off YOUR FUCKING WITH THE LORE OF THE SWORD!!! WTF! If Richard doesn't beleive in the sword than he can;t kill with it... theres no BS about the anger going away and he being able to just use it like a normal ass sword. if he doesn't beleive in it, he can't hit anything with it.<br />come on now.. i don't mind terry changing up shit like that for the point of the story, but you better god damn acknowledge that theres something funky going on with the swords magic that's letting him just use it as a normal sword.<br /><br />I forgot what the other big problem was.. maybe if i remember i'll come back and add it here... it wasn't nearly as big as fucking up the sword though.<br /><br />Actually maybe i have three things? because I don't think this is it, but have they ever said that the gift can't heal poison? because it seems like it should be able to, and if it can't then put in like a 1 sentence explanation why not. I don't remember one in the past, but that doesn't mean there isn't one in one of the previous books... but they fucking repeat every single piece of lore possible so there's no way if they did say it in the past they wouldn't have retold it this book.<br /><br />alright, anyway, the slide was cool I guess, good that they had another mini end boss before they take on ja-gang... I liked it as a small middle of the series book, nothing super important happened, a dude was made and a dude was killed.<br /><br />its a little weird how this old ass book has some obvious parallels to identity politics in today's climate though... I enjoyed that, I guess you always assume that the first time you hear about shit is the first time its come up, but I guess not... were just discussing common ass problems with new words.<br /><br />ah yea! while were talking about the political BS... god damn terry can you tone it down?? like just imply some shit dont fucking take 45 fucking pages to tell us about your political agenda... god damn that shit gets tedious.<br /><br />also I remembered the other things that bothered me.. the little statue of Richard with it turning to black glass... did his sister grab it? how did she grab it? i feel like they never addressed how he got it, and how it got down from the first statue, and how little the whole thing meant because he just broke it like 2 scenes later...<br />don't add in shit that doesn't matter Terry.... and if it did matter then my bad I wasn't paying enough attention.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17813434824401797681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vWsnG+Yb3ZZesSqsLjO32hBrGZgbY3CLBu11jtAyy1hcxhcr8btU59tbDzFdgEJUw0iznO1AZh6uSjmyT4ZVeQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer12030728668662647193">Terry Goodkind was a contemporary American writer and author of the best-selling epic fantasy series, <i>The Sword of Truth</i>, creator of the television show <i>The Legend of the Seeker</i>, and writer of the self-published epic, <i>The First Confessor: The Legend of Magda Searus</i> (a prequel and origin story of the first Mother Confessor). He had over 20 million copies in print and has been translated into more t</span>
  <span id="freeText12030728668662647193" style="display:none">Terry Goodkind was a contemporary American writer and author of the best-selling epic fantasy series, <i>The Sword of Truth</i>, creator of the television show <i>The Legend of the Seeker</i>, and writer of the self-published epic, <i>The First Confessor: The Legend of Magda Searus</i> (a prequel and origin story of the first Mother Confessor). He had over 20 million copies in print and has been translated into more than 20 different languages, world-wide.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/terrygoodkind">http://www.facebook.com/terrygoodkind</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/terrygoodkind">http://www.twitter.com/terrygoodkind</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.vimeo.com/terrygoodkind">http://www.vimeo.com/terrygoodkind</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.terrygoodkind.com">http://www.terrygoodkind.com</a></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1443364-naked-empire-sword-of-truth-8">Quotes from Naked Empire</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;If you are unwilling to defend your right to your own lives,<br /> then you are merely like mice trying to argue with owls.<br /> You think their ways are wrong.<br /> They think you are dinner.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/157528-if-you-are-unwilling-to-defend-your-right-to-your">98 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;People use democracy as a free-floating abstraction disconnected from reality. Democracy in and of itself is not necessarily good. Gang rape, after all, is democracy in action.<br /><br />All men have the right to live their own life. Democracy must be rooted in a rational philosophy that first and foremost recognizes the right of an individual. A few million Imperial Order men screaming for the lives of a much smaller number of people in the New World may win a democratic vote, but it does not give them the right to those lives, or make their calls for such killing right.<br /><br />Democracy is not a synonym for justice or for freedom. Democracy is not a sacred right sanctifying mob rule. Democracy is a principle that is subordinate to the inalienable rights of the individual.&rdquo;</span>
